1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Compliance Audit: Kafka Audit Logging and Authorization Events

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in `apache/kafka` that produce audit log entries for authorization decisions. Search `core/src/main/scala/` and `clients/src/main/java/` for files that log `ALLOWED` or `DENIED` authorization events, reference `AuditLogger`, or implement audit trail functionality for ACL decisions. Report the file path and the class name producing audit events.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I have completed my analysis of the Apache Kafka codebase to find all Java source files that produce audit log entries for authorization decisions.

## Summary

I've identified the key files that produce audit log entries for authorization decisions in Apache Kafka:

### **Main Findings:**

1. **StandardAuthorizerData.java** (`metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/metadata/authorizer/StandardAuthorizerData.java`)
   - Contains the `logAuditMessage()` method that logs both ALLOWED and DENIED authorization events
   - Uses `buildAuditMessage()` to construct detailed audit messages including principal, operation, resource, host, and authorization decision
   - Uses logger "kafka.authorizer.logger" for audit trail entries

2. **StandardAuthorizer.java** (`metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/metadata/authorizer/StandardAuthorizer.java`)
   - The built-in Kafka authorizer implementation that uses StandardAuthorizerData internally
   - Delegates authorization checks to StandardAuthorizerData which triggers audit logging

The audit logging mechanism logs authorization decisions at different levels:
- **ALLOWED**: DEBUG level (if logIfAllowed is true), otherwise TRACE
- **DENIED**: INFO level (if logIfDenied is true), otherwise TRACE

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details about these audit logging classes and their functionality.

\\n219:     /**\\n220:      * Authorize an action based on the current set of ACLs.\\n221:      *\\n222:      * In order to know whether to allow or deny the action, we need to examine the ACLs\\n223:      * that apply to it. If any DENY ACLs match, the operation is denied, no matter how\\n224:      * many ALLOW ACLs match. If neither ALLOW nor DENY ACLs match, we return the default\\n225:      * result. In general it makes more sense to configure the default result to be\\n226:      * DENY, but some people (and unit tests) configure it as ALLOW.\\n227:      */\\n228:     public AuthorizationResult authorize(\\n229:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\\n230:         Action action\\n231:     ) {\\n232:         if (action.resourcePattern().patternType() != LITERAL) {\\n233:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Only literal resources are supported. So log only at trace level.\\n292:                 if (action.logIfAllowed() && auditLog.isDebugEnabled()) {\\n293:                     auditLog.debug(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n294:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n295:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n296:                 }\\n297:                 return;\\n298: \\n299:             case DENIED:\\n300:                 // logIfDenied is true if access to the resource was explicitly requested. Since this is an attempt\\n301:                 // to access unauthorized resources, log at info level. If false, this is either a request to determine\\n302:                 // authorized operations or a filter (e.g for regex subscriptions) to filter out authorized resources.\\n303:                 // In this case, log only at trace level.\\n304:                 if (action.logIfDenied()) {\\n305:                     auditLog.info(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n306: }\\n310:     }\\n311: \\n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\\n314:         String host,\\n315:         Action action\\n316:     ) {\\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which exemplar.resourceName().substring(0, matchesUpTo),\\n415:                     exemplar.patternType(),\\n416:                     exemplar.principal(),\\n417:
